                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">غَرَّهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَغُرُّ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">غُرُورٌ</foreign> (Fr, S, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">غَرٌّ</foreign>, (Az, K,) which latter is preferable to the former, [though less common,] because the inf. n. of a trans. verb is scarcely ever of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فُعُولٌ</foreign>, (Az,) and <foreign lang="ar">غِرَّةٌ</foreign> (Lh, K) and <foreign lang="ar">غَرَرٌ</foreign>, (IKtt, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (the devil, TA) <hi rend="ital">deceived him; beguiled him;</hi> (S, K;) <hi rend="ital">made him to desire what was vain,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">false.</hi> (K.) You say <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّتْهُ الدُّنْيَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The world deceived him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beguiled him, by its finery,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">show,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pomp.</hi> (Msb.) It is said in the Kur [lxxxii. 6], <foreign lang="ar">مَا غَرَّكَ بِرَبِّكَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">What hath deceived thee, and led thee into error, so that thou hast neglected what was incumbent on thee to thy Lord?</hi> (Aboo-Is-hák:) or <hi rend="ital">what hath deceived thee respecting thy Lord, and induced thee to disobey Him, and to feel secure from his punishment?</hi> (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">what hath deceived thee, and emboldened thee to disobey thy Lord?</hi> (Bd. [But see <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign> as syn. with <foreign lang="ar">عَنْ</foreign>.]) <foreign lang="ar">مَا غَرَّكَ بِفُلَانٍ</foreign> signifies [<hi rend="ital">What hath deceived thee, and emboldened thee against such a one?</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">how is it that thou art emboldened against such a one?</hi> (As, S, Msb, TA.) [See also 4.] And <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّكَ بِفُلَانٍ</foreign>, (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ فُلَانٍ</foreign>, (S, TA,) <hi rend="ital">Who hath made thee to pursue a course without being rightly directed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a course not plain,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">مَنْ أَوْطَأَكَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عُشْوَةً</foreign>, S, TA,) <hi rend="ital">with respect to such a one,</hi> (S,) or <hi rend="ital">with respect to the case of such a one?</hi> (TA. [See again 4.]) [Also <foreign lang="ar">غُرَّ مِنْ فُلَانٍ</foreign>, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">غُرَّ غُرُورًا صَادِرًا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ فُلَانٍ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He was deceived by such a one; he was deceived with deceit proceeding from such a one.</hi> See <foreign lang="ar">غَرِيرٌ</foreign>, as syn. with <foreign lang="ar">مَغْرُورٌ</foreign>.] And <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّ فُلَانٌ فُلَانًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Such a one exposed such a one to perdition</hi> or <hi rend="ital">destruction</hi> [app. <hi rend="ital">by deceiving him</hi>]. (TA. [See also 2, and 4.]) Also <hi rend="ital">Such a one acted with such a one in a manner resembling the slaying with the edge of the sword.</hi> (TA. [See 3 in art. <foreign lang="ar">عطو</foreign>.])       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّ فَرْخَهُ</foreign>, (S, O, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="garu3a">غَرُرَ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, O,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">غَرٌّ</foreign> (S, O, K) and <foreign lang="ar">غِرَارٌ</foreign>, (O, K, [or the latter is inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">غَارَّ</foreign> only,]) <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a bird, S, O, K, * or a pigeon, TA) <hi rend="ital">fed its young one with its bill:</hi> (S, O, K:) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n31577-1" target="غارّ" n="1" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>أُنْثَاهُ</foreign>, (As, S, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">غِرَارٌ</foreign> (S) or <foreign lang="ar">مُغَارَّةٌ</foreign>, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">he</hi> (the [collared turtle-dove called] <foreign lang="ar">قُمْرِىّ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">fed his female with his bill.</hi> (As, S, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Hence, in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">كَانَ يَغُرُّ عَلِيًّا</foreign> (O, TA) <foreign lang="ar">بِالعِلْمِ</foreign> (TA) <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (the Prophet) <hi rend="ital">used to nourish 'Alee with knowledge like as the bird feeds its young one.</hi> (O, TA. *) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">غُرَّ فُلَانٌ مِنَ العِلْمِ مَا لَمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يُغَرُّهُ غَيْرُهُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Such a one has been nourished,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">instructed, with that wherewith other than he has not been nourished,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">instructed, of knowledge.</hi> (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَغِرُّ</foreign>, (S, Msb,) with kesr; (S;) or <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّ</foreign>, see. pers. <foreign lang="ar">غَرِرْتَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَغَرُّ</foreign>; (K, TA;) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">غَرَارَةٌ</foreign>; (S, Msb, K;) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a man, S, Msb, or a youth, or young man, K) <hi rend="ital">was inexperienced in affairs;</hi> (S, K;) <hi rend="ital">he was ignorant of affairs; negligent,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">heedless, of them.</hi> (Msb.) You say <foreign lang="ar">كَانَ ذٰلِكَ فِى غَرَارَتِى وَحَدَاثَتِى</foreign>, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">فِى غِرَّتِى</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">That was in</hi> [the time of] <hi rend="ital">my inexperience and youth.</hi> (S.) [See also 8.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّ</foreign>, (K,) see. pers. <foreign lang="ar">غَررْتَ</foreign>, (IAar, T, TA,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَغَرُّ</foreign>, with fet-h, (IAar, T, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">غَرَارَةٌ</foreign>, (IAar, T, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He acted in a youthful</hi> or <hi rend="ital">childish manner:</hi> (IAar, T, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">he so acted after having soundness of judgment, produced by experience.</hi> (Sgh, K.) But this is at variance with what J cites from Fr, in art. <foreign lang="ar">شد</foreign>, that the aor. of an intrans. verb of this class of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلَ</foreign>, should be of the measure <foreign lang="ar">يَفْعِلُ</foreign>, with kesr to the <foreign lang="ar">ع</foreign>. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="4">-A4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّ</foreign>, (IAar, IKtt, K,) in one place written by IAar <foreign lang="ar">غَرِرَ</foreign>, to show that it is of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعِلَ</foreign>, and that the sec. pers. is <foreign lang="ar">غَرِرْتَ</foreign>, (TA,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَغَرُّ</foreign>, (IAar, IKtt, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">غَرَرٌ</foreign> (IAar, K) and <foreign lang="ar">غُرَّةٌ</foreign>, (IAar, IKtt, K,) or the latter, as ISd thinks, is not an inf. n., but a subst., (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">غَراَرَةٌ</foreign>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a horse, IAar, IKtt, and a camel, IAar) <hi rend="ital">had what is termed a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">غُرَّة</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">upon his forehead:</hi> (IAar, IKtt:) <hi rend="ital">it</hi> (his face) <hi rend="ital">had what is so termed:</hi> (K:) <hi rend="ital">it</hi> (his face) <hi rend="ital">became white.</hi> (IAar, K. *)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَغَرُّ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a man) <hi rend="ital">became eminent,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">noble.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">غُرَّةٌ</foreign> signifies also A grape-vine's <hi rend="ital">quickly becoming tall.</hi> (K.)       <sense type="A" n="5">-A5-</sense>  See also R. Q. 1.       <sense type="A" n="6">-A6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">غَرَّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَآءَ</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">Very deceitful;</hi> applied in this sense as an epithet to the present world; (Msb;) or <hi rend="ital">what deceives one;</hi> (K;) such as a man, and a devil, or other thing; (As, TA;) or such as property or wealth, and rank or station, and desire, and a devil: (B, TA:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n31592-1" target="غُرُورٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n31593"/></foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">a thing by which one is deceived,</hi> of worldly goods or advantages: (S:) or the former signifies the <hi rend="ital">devil,</hi> specially; (Yaakoob, S, K;) because he deceives men by false promises and by inspiring hopes; or because he urges a man to do those things which are causes of his being loved but which are followed by that which grieves him: (TA:) and this last sense it has, accord. to ISk, in the Kur xxxi. 33 and xxxv. 5: (S:) also the <hi rend="ital">present world;</hi> (K;) as an epithet in which the quality of a subst. predominates: and this sense is assigned to it by some as used in the passages of the Kur-án to which reference has just been made.                   <hi rend="ital">Deceived; beguiled; made to desire what is vain,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">false;</hi> (A'Obeyd, K;) and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n31594-1" target="مَغْرُورٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n31600"/></foreign>. (K.)       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n31594-3" target="مَغْرُورٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n31600"/></foreign> signifies also A man <hi rend="ital">who marries to a woman in the belief that she is free, and finds her to be a slave.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">غِرٌّ</foreign>, in three places.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  It is said in a prov., <foreign lang="ar">أَنَا غَرِيرُكَ مِنْ هٰذَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَمْرِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">I am one possessing knowledge in this affair so that when thou askest me of it I will inform thee respecting it without being prepared for it and without consideration:</hi> so says AZ: and Z says the like; i. e. <hi rend="ital">I</hi> [<hi rend="ital">am one who</hi>] <hi rend="ital">will answer thee if thou ask me unexpectedly respecting this affair by reason of the soundness of my knowledge of the true state of the case:</hi> or [it means <hi rend="ital">I am a deceived informant of thee respecting this affair;</hi> for] as As says, the meaning is, thou art not deceived by me, but I am the person deceived; the case being this, that false information came to me, and I acquainted thee with it, and it was not as I told thee; I having only related what I had heard. (TA.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">أَنَا غَرِيرُكَ مِنْهُ</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">I caution thee</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">I am thy cautioner</hi>] <hi rend="ital">against him;</hi> (K, TA:) [i. e.,] <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ فُلَانٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">against such a one</hi>]; (S, O;) meaning, as Aboo-Nasr says in the “ Kitáb el-Ajnás, ” [<hi rend="ital">that</hi>] <hi rend="ital">there shall not happen to thee, from him, that whereby thou shalt be deceived;</hi> (S, O, TA;) as though he said, <hi rend="ital">I am thy surety,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sponsor, for that.</hi> (AM, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [Hence, app., it is said that] <foreign lang="ar">غَرِيرٌ</foreign> signifies also <hi rend="ital">A surety, sponsor,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">guarantee.</hi> (K, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">عَيْشٌ غَرِيرٌ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">A life in which one is not made to be in fear:</hi> (S, K, TA:) like <foreign lang="ar">عَيْشٌ أَبْلَهُ</foreign>: (TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">غُرَّانٌ</foreign>.
